Topic: Surgery
Question: Obstructive sleep apnoea caused by the following
Choices:
  A: Mandibular ameloblasma
  B: Dentigerous cyst
  C: Orbital fracture
  D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Obstructive sleep apnoea is a sleep disorder where breathing repeatedly stops and starts during sleep.
  Any physical obstruction that narrows or blocks the upper airway can contribute to snoring and sleep apnea.
  Mandibular ameloblastoma is a rare, benign tumor arising from odontogenic epithelium, and can cause jaw swelling and pain but not obstructive sleep apnea.
  Dentigerous cyst, also known as follicular cyst of the jaw, is a developmental odontogenic cyst present around the crown of an unerupted tooth and does not cause obstructive sleep apnea.
  Orbital fracture is trauma to the bone around the eye socket and may cause double vision or inability to move the eye, but it does not directly cause sleep apnea.
  Bilateral TMJ ankylosis can cause mouth opening restriction and breathing difficulties, and may contribute to sleep apnea.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought: 
Obstructive sleep apnea occurs due to obstruction (blockage) of the airway during sleep.
Mandibular ameloblastoma and dentigerous cyst are not related to airway obstruction.
Orbital fracture usually does not cause airway obstruction.
Bilateral TMJ ankylosis may cause airway obstruction due to the limited movement of the mandible.
Therefore, the answer is D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis.
Action: Answer("D")

  D: Atorvastatin 80 mg

  Based on the lipid levels, the patient has hypertriglyceridemia, which is a risk factor for cardiovascular disease.
  The preferred treatment for hypertriglyceridemia includes fibrate medications, such as Fenofibrate.
  However, the patient also has borderline high LDL levels, which indicate that he may also benefit from a statin medication.
  Combination therapy, such as Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate, has been shown to be effective in reducing the risk of cardiovascular events in patients with high triglycerides and low HDL levels.
  Therefore, the best option for this patient would be Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate.
  The other options, Fenofibrate alone, Rosuvastatin 10 mg, and Atorvastatin 80 mg, may not provide adequate reduction in triglycerides or may not be safe for the patient given his history of myocardial infarction and age.

Topic: Anatomy
Question: Which of the following structure is not present on floor of third ventricle?
Choices:
  A: Optic stalk
  B: Third nerve
  C: Infundibulum
  D: Mammillary body
Response 0:
Thought: 
The third ventricle is a narrow slit-like cavity between the two thalami, situated from the optic chiasma anteriorly to the cerebral aqueduct posteriorly.
The optic stalk is present on the floor of the third ventricle.
The third nerve and infundibulum are also present on the floor of the third ventricle.
The mammillary body is not present on the floor of the third ventricle. It lies posterior to it, on the posterior perforated substance.
Therefore, the answer is D: Mammillary body.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  The floor of the third ventricle is formed by hypothalamus and some of its structures.
  Optic stalk and infundibulum are present on the floor of the third ventricle.
  Third nerve exits through the opening between the cerebral peduncles, which are located anterior to the hypothalamus.
  Mammillary bodies are located posterior to the hypothalamus.
  Therefore, third nerve is not present on the floor of the third ventricle.
Action: Answer("B")

  The mammillary body is a pair of small, round structures located on the undersurface of the brain.
  Therefore, the structure that is NOT present on the floor of the third ventricle should be either the optic stalk, the third nerve, or the mammillary body.
  The infundibulum, however, is located on the floor of the third ventricle.
  Therefore, the answer is C: Infundibulum.

Choices:

  D: Child less than 2 years

Cystic fibrosis patients are prone to infections due to a weakened immune system.
Sickle cell anemia patients are also at an increased risk of infections.
Patients with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis are at an increased risk of sinus infections but PPV-23 is not the primary vaccine for them.
Children less than 2 years are at a higher risk of pneumococcal infections, but there are other vaccines recommended for them.
Based on this, it seems like the vaccine would be most beneficial for either A or B.

  Recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis suggest chronic sinus infections.

  Therefore, the best choice would be C: the patient with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis.

  Quadritubercular refers to molars with four cusps or tubercles.
  Haplodont teeth have a single cusp and are typically found in small mammals.
  Triconodont teeth have three main cusps and are found in extinct mammals.
  Mandibular Molars have four to five cusps, which means they are quadritubercular.
  Therefore, the answer is B: Quadritubercular teeth.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 7:
Thought:  
    Mandibular molar is a type of tooth.
    Haplodont teeth have a low, round, or blunt crown.
    Tritubercular teeth have three cusps.
    Triconodont teeth have a single cusp, and they are arranged in a straight line.
    Therefore, the answer is B: Quadritubercular teeth.
Action: Answer("B")

Question: Which of following is an oral precancer?
Choices:
  A: Oral hairy Leukoplakia
  B: White spongy naevus
  C: Leukemia
  D: Speckled Leukoplakia
Response 0:
Thought: 
- Oral precancer refers to a condition that has the potential to cause cancer in the oral cavity. 
- Oral hairy Leukoplakia is a benign, asymptomatic white plaque-like lesion usually on the lateral border of the tongue. It is caused by the Epstein-Barr virus, and it is common in people with immunosuppression, such as people with HIV. Although it is not cancerous, it is considered a marker of immune suppression.
- White spongy naevus is a rare hereditary disease, characterized by soft white patches that appear on the oral mucosa. It is not a precancerous lesion.
- Leukemia is a type of cancer that affects the blood and bone marrow, it is not a precancerous lesion of the oral cavity. 
- Speckled Leukoplakia is a white and red patch that has a higher risk of cancer transformation than other types of leukoplakia. It usually affects the lateral border of the tongue, and it is commonly associated with tobacco and alcohol use. It is considered a precancerous lesion. 
- Therefore, the answer is D: Speckled Leukoplakia.

  B: Rutherford-Morrison incision
  C: Pfannenstiel incision
  D: Lanz incision
Response 0:
Thought:
A muscle splitting incision refers to a surgical approach that involves the separation of muscle fibers along the anatomical direction of the fibers, rather than cutting through them.
Kocher's incision is a standard incision for accessing the gallbladder and bile ducts, which runs along the right subcostal margin.
Rutherford-Morrison Incision is made in the right iliac fossa and is commonly used in appendectomy, salpingo-oophorectomy (removal of ovary and fallopian tube), or sigmoidectomy surgeries.
Pfannenstiel incision is a curved incision made below the navel, which is often used in gynecological and urologic surgeries.
Lanz incision is a transverse incision made in the right lower quadrant of the abdomen and is usually used in appendectomy surgeries.
Therefore, the muscle splitting incision is not Kocher's, Rutherford-Morrison, Pfannenstiel, or Lanz incision.

Choices:
  A: Guiding cusps.
  B: Supporting cusps.
  C: Holding cusps.
  D: Balancing cusps.
Response 0:
Thought:
  A cusp is a raised or pointed part on the chewing surface of a tooth.
  Working cusps are the cusps that make contact during jaw movement to facilitate grinding and chewing of food.
  Guiding cusps are the cusps that guide the mandibular movement in a particular direction.
  Supporting cusps are located on the opposite side of working cusps and help to support the food bolus during the chewing process.
  Holding cusps are not a commonly used term when referring to dental anatomy.
  Balancing cusps are also not a commonly used term when referring to dental anatomy.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Guiding cusps.
Action: Answer("A")

  Guiding cusps are the cusps of the upper teeth that contact the opposing tooth during mandibular excursion.
  Supporting cusps are the cusps of the lower teeth that support the bite or vertical dimension of occlusion.
  Holding cusps is not a dental terminology.
  Balancing cusps are the cusps of the upper teeth that contact the opposing tooth in lateral or side-to-side movement.
  Therefore, working cusps are also known as guiding cusps.

Topic: Dental
Question: A lateral sliding flap done on a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years will show
Choices:
  A: PDL fibres attached to cementum
  B: PDL fibres attached to dentin
  C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface
  D: Co adaptation to the remaining fibres
Response 0:
Thought:
  A lateral sliding flap is a technique for Periodontal surgery.
  Roots denuded for 6 years means that the tooth has been exposed to the oral environment for a long time.
  The PDL fibers are the fibers that attach the cementum to the Alveolar bone.
  If the roots are denuded, the PDL fibers may have been destroyed and the attachment between the cementum and the alveolar bone lost.
  Based on the above information, the answer is unlikely to be option A or B.
  If the tooth roots have been denuded, the epithelium (tissue covering the tooth) may have moved inwards to cover the exposed root surface.
  Co-adaptation refers to the adaption of fibers to a new surface.
  Therefore, the answer is C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  A lateral sliding flap is a periodontal surgical procedure done to access and treat a root surface of teeth.
  Root denudation occurs when the tooth's roots are exposed to the oral environment.
  If roots are denuded for a long time, the periodontal ligament (PDL) fibres will be destroyed.
  In the lateral sliding flap procedure, the PDL fibres are undermined and repositioned coronally.
  Therefore, PDL fibres will not be attached to the underlying denuded root surface.
  However, new PDL fibres can reattach to a previously denuded root surface after some time.
  Co adaptation of the remaining fibres may occur if there are any remaining PDL fibres.
  Epithelium will normally migrate towards its previous location if there is a coronal movement of the tooth.
  Therefore, the most possible answer is C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought: 
  A lateral sliding flap is an approach to access the root of a tooth and repair it.
  Roots that have been denuded for 6 years means that the roots have been exposed to the oral environment without any intervention for a long time.
  In such a case, it is possible that there will be damage to the periodontal ligament (PDL) fibers that attach the tooth to the bone.
  If the PDL fibers are damaged, they may not be able to fully reattach to the root during healing.
  Therefore, it is possible that PDL fibres may become attached to the cementum or dentin as the tooth tries to heal.
  Since the root has been denuded for a long time, it is also possible for epithelium to be adjacent to the previously denuded root surface.
  Co adaptation to the remaining fibres is not a known result of a lateral sliding flap.
  Therefore, the answer is either A, B, or C.
  Since PDL fibers can attach to both cementum or dentin, the most specific answer would be B: PDL fibres attached to dentin.

Question: Which of the following has least density?
Choices:
  A: VLDL
  B: LDL
  C: HDL
  D: Chylomicrons
Response 0:
Thought:
Density is inversely proportional to size.
Chylomicrons are the largest lipoprotein particles and have the least density.
VLDL (Very Low-Density Lipoprotein) particles are the second-largest lipoprotein particles.
LDL (Low-Density Lipoprotein) particles are smaller than VLDL particles.
HDL (High-Density Lipoprotein) particles are the smallest particles among them all.
Therefore, the answer is C: HDL has least density.

Topic: Dental
Question: Multi constricted apical constriction is seen in which type of Dummerâ€™s classification
Choices:
  A: Type 1
  B: Type 2
  C: Type 3
  D: Type 4
Response 0:
Thought:
  Dummer's classification is a method to classify the root canal configuration in mandibular first molars.
  In type 1, two separate canals are present in both mesial and distal roots.
  In type 2, a single canal is present in mesial root, while two separate canals are present in distal root.
  In type 3, a single canal is present in distal root, while two separate canals are present in both mesial roots.
  In type 4, only one canal is present in both mesial and distal roots.
  Multi-constricted apical constriction implies multiple points of narrowing at the apical end of the canal.
  Type 4 canal configuration typically has a single apical constriction.
  Therefore, the answer is not Type 4.
  As there is no specific mention of multiple canals in any of the type 1, type 2, or type 3 categories, it is unclear which one is the correct answer.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The question refers to Dummer's classification, which is a classification system for the anatomy of the root canal system.
  Multi-constricted apical constriction means there are multiple areas of constriction near the apex of the root.
  Looking at Dummerâ€™s classification, this is typically seen in Type 3.
  Therefore, the answer is C: Type 3.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought:
  Dummer's classification is used for the complexity of root canal system.
  Multi constricted apical constriction means that there are multiple apical constrictions in a root canal.
  Type 1 means a single and straight canal that has one main foramen.
  Type 2 means two separate canals merge into one canal before exiting via one apical foramen.
  Type 3 means there are one or two lateral canals on the apical third of the root canal.
  Type 4 means there are multiple apical foramina and/or apical delta.

  A: Glycolysis
  B: Glycogenolysis
  C: TCA cycle
  D: Phosphocreatine
Response 0:

  Resynthesis of ATP is essential for muscle contraction during short-term, high-intensity exercise.
  Phosphocreatine is a rapidly available energy source that helps regenerate ATP from ADP.
  Glycolysis and glycogenolysis are also involved in the production of ATP, but they take longer to produce ATP than phosphocreatine.
  TCA cycle is more involved in aerobic metabolism for long duration exercises.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Phosphocreatine.

  Therefore, semi colon shaped C-shaped canal should fall under one of the classifications specified by Melton and Seitzor.
  Among the given choices:
  - Type 1 classification is for round/oval canals
  - Type 2 classification is for two separate canals
  - Type 3 classification is for a single canal with an irregular shape

  The canal may assume a linear, curved, or semi-circular course.
  A C-shaped canal has a mesiodistal groove separating the canals forming the shape of a C or semi-colon.

  Syphilis is a sexually transmitted infection caused by the bacteria Treponema pallidum, and it often presents with skin rashes but not with "Strawberry Tongue".
  Measles is a highly contagious disease caused by the measles virus, which usually produces Koplik spots on the buccal mucosa instead of "Strawberry Tongue".
  Scarlet fever is a bacterial illness that develops in some people who have strep throat, and it is characterised by a red rash on the skin, sore throat and "Strawberry Tongue".
  Typhoid is a bacterial infection caused by Salmonella typhi, which commonly presents with fever, headache, and abdominal pain but not necessarily with "Strawberry Tongue".
  Therefore, the answer is C: scarlet fever.

Question: Which of the following instructions should be given to a lactating mother regarding drug usage?
Choices:
  A: No advice is required as most of the drugs are secreted negligibly in the milk
  B: Take drugs with longer half-life
  C: Tell her to feed the baby just before next dose
  D: Do not feed the baby if you are consuming any drug
Response 0:
Thought:
  Lactating mothers should take special care while consuming medication.
  A: No advice is required as most of the drugs are secreted negligibly in the milk - This statement is not true as many drugs can pass through the milk and can cause harm to the baby.
  B: Taking drugs with longer half-life is not a solution for this problem.
  C: Telling the mother to feed the baby just before the next dose, ensures that the concentration of the drug in the milk will be at its lowest when the baby is feeding.
  D: Instructing mothers not to feed the baby if they're consuming any drug is incorrect.
  
Therefore, the most appropriate advice for lactating mothers is to feed the baby just before the next dose.  The correct answer is C. 

Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Drugs taken by lactating mothers may enter into the breast milk and affect the infant.
  Some drugs may adversely affect the growth and development of the infant.
  Some drugs may also interfere with lactation.
  Drugs with a shorter half-life should be preferred.
  If the dose of the drug causes drowsiness in the mother, then the infant should not be breastfed.
  Feeding the baby before the dose or at a time when the concentration of the drug in the milk is low is a safe option.
  Therefore, the correct option is C: Tell her to feed the baby just before the next dose.
  
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought: 
  Lactating mothers need to be cautious while consuming medications as it may get into the milk.
  Many drugs are secreted negligibly in the milk and are safe to consume.
  Longer half-life drugs may accumulate in breast milk and may cause side effects in infants.
  It is better to avoid drugs that are not necessary.
  If medication is necessary, advise taking the medication just after breastfeeding the baby, allowing the time interval of at least 2-3 hours before the next feed.
  Therefore, option A is incorrect as not all drugs are secreted negligibly in the milk.
  Option B is incorrect since longer half-life drugs are not recommended.
  Option D is incorrect as complete avoidance of breastfeeding is not required for all medications.
  The correct answer is C: Tell her to feed the baby just before taking the next dose.

  Linagliptin is a DPP-4 inhibitor and is primarily excreted unchanged in feces; thus, no renal dose adjustment is required.
  Repaglinide is a meglitinide and requires dose adjustment if CrCl is <40 ml/min.
  Vildagliptin is also a DPP-4 inhibitor and needs to be used cautiously with renal impairment.
  Glimepiride is a sulfonylurea and would require a decrease in the dose or frequency of administration in patients with decreased renal function.
  Therefore, the preferred oral hypoglycemic agent in this patient will be Linagliptin.

Question: The patients with class II division 1 malocclusion have
Choices:
  A: Hypertonic Lower Lip
  B: Hypotonic Lower lip
  C: Hypertonic upper Lip
  D: Hypotonic upper lip
Response 0:
Thought:
  Malocclusion class II division 1 describes an abnormal buccolingual relationship between the maxillary central incisors and the mandibular anterior teeth and an abnormal anteroposterior relationship between maxilla and mandible.
  Patients with malocclusion class II division 1 have a skeletal discrepancy between maxilla and mandible.
  Skeletal/jaw discrepancies may result in changes to facial muscles, especially the lips, tongue, and cheeks.
  Typically, patients with class II division 1 malocclusion have a convex facial profile and a retruded mandible.
  Therefore, the patients with class II division 1 malocclusion most likely have a hypertonic upper lip.
Answer: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  Class II division 1 malocclusion is a type of malocclusion.
  Hypertonic refers to overly tight or tense muscles.
  Hypotonic refers to overly loose or relaxed muscles.
  Class II division 1 malocclusion is characterized by the upper teeth being further forward relative to the lower teeth.
  This means there is an overjet and retruded lower jaw.
  The lower lip will be under-stimulated and hypotonic due to retruded lower jaw.
  Therefore, the patients with class II division 1 malocclusion have a hypotonic lower lip.

  Therefore, patients with class II division 1 malocclusion are likely to have a Hypotonic Lower lip.

  For etching porcelain, hydrofluoric acid (HF) is used.
  The concentration of hydrofluoric acid used for etching porcelain is typically between 4 to 9.6%.
  A concentration of 1.23% HF is used for etching enamel, not porcelain.
  37% HF is too strong for etching porcelain and can damage it.
  Therefore, the most appropriate concentration of HF for etching porcelain is between 4 to 9.6%.

  The concentration of HF used for porcelain etching varies, but it is typically less than the concentration used for metal etching.
